KUBERNETES - Basic Signal Handler Pattern\n\n### File: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go`\n```go\n// SetupSignalContext returns a context that is cancelled on SIGTERM or SIGINT\nfunc SetupSignalContext() context.Context {\n    close(onlyOneSignalHandler) // panic if called twice\n    \n    shutdownHandler = make(chan os.Signal, 2)\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    \n    signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)\n    go func() {\n        <-shutdownHandler           // First signal cancels context\n        cancel()\n        <-shutdownHandler           // Second signal exits immediately\n        os.Exit(1)\n    }()\n    \n    return ctx\n}\n```\n\n### File: `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go`\n```go\nvar shutdownSignals = []os.Signal{os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM}\n```\n\n### Key Principles:\n- Single signal handler ensures no duplicate registrations\n- 2-capacity channel prevents losing signals\n- First signal triggers graceful shutdown\n- Second signal force-exits with code 1\n- Returns context for dependency tracking\n\n---\n\n## 2. KUBERNETES - Advanced Interrupt Handler\n\n### File: `pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go`\n```go\nvar terminationSignals = []os.Signal{\n    syscall.SIGHUP, syscall.SIGINT, syscall.SIGTERM, syscall.SIGQUIT\n}\n\ntype Handler struct {\n    notify []func()              // Cleanup functions\n    final  func(os.Signal)       // Final handler (default: os.Exit(1))\n    once   sync.Once             // Ensure single execution\n}\n\n// Run wraps the critical section with cleanup guarantee\nfunc (h *Handler) Run(fn func() error) error {\n    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(ch, terminationSignals...)\n    defer func() {\n        signal.Stop(ch)\n        close(ch)\n    }()\n    \n    go func() {\n        sig, ok := <-ch\n        if !ok {\n            return\n        }\n        h.Signal(sig)  // Executes all notify functions\n    }()\n    \n    defer h.Close()    // Ensures cleanup on normal exit\n    return fn()        // Run protected code\n}\n```\n\n### Key Principles:\n- sync.Once ensures cleanup runs exactly once\n- Multiple notification functions run in order\n- Cleanup guaranteed even on panic\n- Signal channel cleaned up properly\n\n---\n\n## 3. KUBERNETES - Leader Election Example\n\n### File: `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/leader-election/main.go`\n```go\nfunc main() {\n    // Create cancellable context for coordinated shutdown\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    defer cancel()\n    \n    // Signal handler with early exit capability\n    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    go func() {\n        <-ch\n        klog.Info(\"Received termination, signaling shutdown\")\n        cancel()  // Triggers leader election cleanup\n    }()\n    \n    // Leader election automatically stops when context is done\n    leaderelection.RunOrDie(ctx, leaderelection.LeaderElectionConfig{\n        Lock: lock,\n        ReleaseOnCancel: true,\n        Callbacks: leaderelection.LeaderCallbacks{\n            OnStartedLeading: func(ctx context.Context) {\n                // Cleanup happens automatically when ctx is cancelled\n                run(ctx)\n            },\n            OnStoppedLeading: func() {\n                // Perform cleanup operations here\n                os.Exit(0)\n            },\n        },\n    })\n}\n```\n\n### Key Principles:\n- Context cancellation coordinates all components\n- Leader election respects context deadline\n- Cleanup callback runs on transition out of leadership\n- No manual cleanup needed if using context properly\n\n---\n\n## 4. PROMETHEUS - Multi-Signal Coordination\n\n### File: `cmd/prometheus/main.go` (lines 1150-1176)\n```go\nvar g run.Group\n\n// Signal handler goroutine\n{\n    term := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    cancel := make(chan struct{})\n    \n    g.Add(\n        // Execution function\n        func() error {\n            select {\n            case sig := <-term:\n                logger.Warn(\"Received an OS signal, exiting gracefully...\", \n                    \"signal\", sig.String())\n                reloadReady.Close()\n            case <-webHandler.Quit():\n                logger.Warn(\"Received termination request via web service, exiting gracefully...\")\n            case <-cancel:\n                reloadReady.Close()\n            }\n            return nil\n        },\n        // Cleanup function\n        func(error) {\n            close(cancel)\n            webHandler.SetReady(web.Stopping)\n            notifs.AddNotification(notifications.ShuttingDown)\n        },\n    )\n}\n\n// Scrape manager with ordered shutdown\n{\n    g.Add(\n        // Execution\n        func() error {\n            err := scrapeManager.Run(discoveryManagerScrape.SyncCh())\n            logger.Info(\"Scrape manager stopped\")\n            return err\n        },\n        // Cleanup - must happen before TSDB close\n        func(error) {\n            logger.Info(\"Stopping scrape manager...\")\n            scrapeManager.Stop()\n        },\n    )\n}\n\n// Run all goroutines until one returns\ng.Run()\n```\n\n### Key Principles:\n- `oklog/run.Group` manages goroutine lifecycle\n- Each g.Add() has execution and cleanup functions\n- All cleanup functions called when any returns\n- Multiple signal sources (OS signal, web API, internal)\n- Cleanup order matters (scrape before TSDB)\n- Context-less but explicit cleanup\n\n---\n\n## 5. err != nil {\n                fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, \"Failed to reload loggers: %s\\n\", err)\n            }\n        case sig := <-signalChan:\n            // Bounded shutdown timeout\n            ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\n            defer cancel()\n            \n            if err := s.Shutdown(ctx, fmt.Sprintf(\"System signal: %s\", sig)); err != nil {\n                fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, \"Timed out waiting for server to shut down\\n\")\n            }\n            return  // Exit signal handler\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### File: `pkg/server/server.go` (lines 155-172)\n```go\nfunc (s *Server) Shutdown(ctx context.Context, reason string) error {\n    var err error\n    s.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n        s.log.Info(\"Shutdown started\", \"reason\", reason)\n        \n        // Call all service shutdown logic\n        if shutdownErr := s.managerAdapter.Shutdown(ctx, \"shutdown\"); shutdownErr != nil {\n            s.log.Error(\"Failed to shutdown background services\", \"error\", shutdownErr)\n        }\n        \n        // Wait for context or timeout\n        select {\n        case <-ctx.Done():\n            s.log.Warn(\"Timed out while waiting for server to shut down\")\n            err = fmt.Errorf(\"timeout waiting for shutdown\")\n        default:\n            s.log.Debug(\"Finished waiting for server to shut down\")\n        }\n    })\n    \n    return err\n}\n```\n\n### File: `pkg/api/http_server.go` (lines 490-497)\n```go\ngo func() {\n    defer wg.Done()\n    \n    <-ctx.Done()\n    // Use background context for HTTP shutdown - don't inherit timeout\n    if err := hs.httpSrv.Shutdown(context.Background()); err != nil {\n        hs.log.Error(\"Failed to shutdown server\", \"error\", err)\n    }\n}()\n\n// Concurrent listener serving\nerrg, _ := errgroup.WithContext(ctx)\nfor _, listener := range listeners {\n    errg.Go(func() error {\n        err := hs.httpSrv.Serve(listener)\n        if errors.Is(err, http.ErrServerClosed) {\n            hs.log.Debug(\"server was shutdown gracefully\")\n            return nil\n        }\n        return err\n    })\n}\n```\n\n### Key Principles:\n- Explicit 30-second shutdown timeout\n- sync.Once ensures single shutdown execution\n- Separate signal channels for different signals (SIGHUP vs SIGTERM)\n- HTTP shutdown uses fresh background context (no timeout inheritance)\n- ErrorGroup manages concurrent listeners\n- Expects http.ErrServerClosed for clean shutdown detection\n\n---\n\n## 6. GRAFANA - Systemd Integration\n\n### File: `pkg/server/server.go` (lines 198-226)\n```go\nfunc (s *Server) notifySystemd(state string) {\n    notifySocket := os.Getenv(\"NOTIFY_SOCKET\")\n    if notifySocket == \"\" {\n        return\n    }\n    \n    socketAddr := &net.UnixAddr{\n        Name: notifySocket,\n        Net:  \"unixgram\",\n    }\n    conn, err := net.DialUnix(socketAddr.Net, nil, socketAddr)\n    if err != nil {\n        s.log.Warn(\"Failed to connect to systemd\", \"err\", err)\n        return\n    }\n    defer func() {\n        if err := conn.Close(); > /tmp/IMPLEMENTATION_GUIDE.md << 'EOF'\n# Go Graceful Shutdown Patterns - Implementation Guide\n\n## Quick Reference\n\nThis guide provides production-ready patterns for implementing graceful shutdown in Go applications, based on analysis of three major production systems: Kubernetes, Prometheus, and Grafana.\n\n### Executive Summary\n\n- **Kubernetes**: Context-based cancellation with panic-on-duplicate signal handler registration\n- **Prometheus**: oklog/run.Group for coordinated multi-component shutdown with explicit cleanup\n- **Grafana**: Explicit timeout (30s) with sync.Once and context-based HTTP server shutdown\n\nAll three use the same core Go signal handling (`os/signal.Notify`), but differ in orchestration and cleanup patterns.\n\n---\n\n## Three Proven Patterns\n\n### Pattern 1: Context-Based (Kubernetes)\n**Best for:** Services with clear component hierarchy  \n**Complexity:** Low  \n**Dependencies:** Standard library only\n\n```go\nctx := setupSignalContext()  // Returns cancelled context on signal\n// Pass ctx to all components\n<-ctx.Done()  // All components stop when ctx cancelled\n```\n\n**Advantages:**\n- Automatic propagation through call stack\n- Simple dependency injection\n- Works with standard context.WithTimeout, context.WithDeadline\n\n**Disadvantages:**\n- Less explicit about cleanup order\n- Harder to coordinate complex dependencies\n\n### Pattern 2: Goroutine Coordination (Prometheus)\n**Best for:** Complex systems with many independent services  \n**Complexity:** Medium  \n**Dependencies:** oklog/run (github.com/oklog/run)\n\n```go\ng := run.Group()\ng.Add(execute func() error, interrupt func(error))\ng.Run()  // Exits when any component returns\n```\n\n**Advantages:**\n- Explicit cleanup functions for each component\n- Clear dependency ordering\n- All cleanups guaranteed to run\n\n**Disadvantages:**\n- Requires external library\n- Steeper learning curve\n- More boilerplate\n\n### Pattern 3: Explicit Timeout (Grafana)\n**Best for:** HTTP services that need bounded shutdown  \n**Complexity:** Medium  \n**Dependencies:** Standard library only\n\n```go\nsignalChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(signalChan, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n<-signalChan\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\nserver.Shutdown(ctx)  // Graceful with timeout\n```\n\n**Advantages:**\n- Explicit timeout prevents hanging processes\n- Clear signal flow\n- Good for HTTP servers\n\n**Disadvantages:**\n- Need to manage multiple signal channels\n- Timeout must be chosen carefully\n- Less flexible for complex scenarios\n\n---\n\n## Signal Configuration Quick Start\n\n### Minimal Implementation\n```go\npackage main\n\nimport (\n    \"context\"\n    \"os\"\n    \"os/signal\"\n    \"syscall\"\n)\n\nfunc setupSignalHandler() context.Context {\n    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    \n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    go func() {\n        sig := <-ch\n        cancel()  // First signal stops the server\n        <-ch\n        os.Exit(1)  // Second signal force-exits\n    }()\n    \n    return ctx\n}\n\nfunc main() {\n    ctx := setupSignalHandler()\n    // Use ctx for all operations\n    <-ctx.Done()\n    cleanup()\n    os.Exit(0)\n}\n```\n\n### With Timeout\n```go\nfunc handleShutdown(server *http.Server) {\n    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    \n    <-ch\n    // Bounded shutdown\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 30*time.Second)\n    defer cancel()\n    \n    if err := server.Shutdown(ctx); err != nil {\n        logger.Error(\"Shutdown timeout\", err)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### With Cleanup Functions\n```go\nfunc main() {\n    handler := interrupt.New(\n        func(sig os.Signal) {\n            logger.Info(\"Shutting down\", \"signal\", sig)\n            os.Exit(0)\n        },\n        func() {\n            logger.Info(\"Cleanup 1\")\n        },\n        func() {\n            logger.Info(\"Cleanup 2\")\n        },\n    )\n    \n    err := handler.Run(func() error {\n        return myServerRun()\n    })\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Shutdown Checklist\n\nWhen implementing graceful shutdown, ensure you handle:\n\n- [ ] **Signal Registration**\n  - [ ] SIGTERM (from containers, systemd)\n  - [ ] SIGINT (from terminal Ctrl+C)\n  - [ ] SIGHUP (for reloading, optional)\n  - [ ] Second signal force-exit\n\n- [ ] **Cleanup Order**\n  - [ ] Stop accepting new connections\n  - [ ] Drain in-flight requests\n  - [ ] Stop background workers\n  - [ ] Flush data to disk/databases\n  - [ ] Close connections/listeners\n\n- [ ] **Timeout Management**\n  - [ ] Set explicit timeout (30-60 seconds recommended)\n  - [ ] Handle timeout with error logging\n  - [ ] Force exit if timeout exceeded\n\n- [ ] **Coordination**\n  - [ ] Prevent duplicate signal handlers\n  - [ ] Ensure cleanup runs exactly once\n  - [ ] Wait for all goroutines to finish\n  - [ ] Log shutdown completion\n\n- [ ] **External Integration**\n  - [ ] Systemd readiness notification (optional)\n  - [ ] Health check endpoint returns not-ready during shutdown\n  - [ ] Load balancer can detect shutdown state\n\n---\n\n## Common Pitfalls and Solutions\n\n### Pitfall 1: Lost Signals\n**Problem:** Signal arrives before handler is registered  \n**Solution:** Register handler early, use buffered channel with size ≥ 1\n\n```go\n// Good\nch := make(chan os.Signal, 2)  // Buffer for multiple signals\nsignal.Notify(ch, ...)\n\n// Bad\nch := make(chan os.Signal)     // Unbuffered - can lose signals\n```\n\n### Pitfall 2: Infinite Wait\n**Problem:** Cleanup blocks forever, process never shuts down  \n**Solution:** Always use context.WithTimeout for external operations\n\n```go\n// Good\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\nserver.Shutdown(ctx)\n\n// Bad\nserver.Shutdown(context.Background())  // No timeout - can hang forever\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Duplicate Shutdown\n**Problem:** Shutdown runs multiple times, corrupting state  \n**Solution:** Use sync.Once for all shutdown code\n\n```go\nvar shutdownOnce sync.Once\n\nfunc shutdown() {\n    shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n        // This code runs exactly once\n    })\n}\n```\n\n### Pitfall 4: Lost Cleanup\n**Problem:** Some goroutines don't see cancellation  \n**Solution:** Always pass context through the call chain\n\n```go\n// Good\nfunc handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {\n    select {\n    case <-ctx.Done():\n        return  // Stops immediately when ctx cancelled\n    case <-time.After(10*time.Second):\n        // Timeout\n    }\n}\n\n// Bad\nfunc handleRequest() {\n    time.Sleep(10*time.Second)  // No way to interrupt\n}\n```\n\n### Pitfall 5: Signal Lost on Double Handling\n**Problem:** Registering signal handler twice leads to unpredictable behavior  \n**Solution:** Use global sync.Once or panic on duplicate\n\n```go\nvar setupOnce sync.Once\n\nfunc setupSignalHandler() {\n    setupOnce.Do(func() {\n        ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n        signal.Notify(ch, ...)\n        // Handler setup\n    })\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Testing Graceful Shutdown\n\n### Unit Test Template\n```go\nfunc TestGracefulShutdown(t *testing.T) {\n    server := startServer()\n    defer server.Close()\n    \n    // Simulate signal\n    go func() {\n        time.Sleep(100*time.Millisecond)\n        syscall.Kill(syscall.Getpid(), syscall.SIGTERM)\n    }()\n    \n    // Server should shut down cleanly\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 5*time.Second)\n    defer cancel()\n    \n    if err := server.Shutdown(ctx); err != nil {\n        t.Fatalf(\"Shutdown failed: %v\", err)\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Integration Test Template\n```go\nfunc TestShutdownWithInFlightRequests(t *testing.T) {\n    server := startServer()\n    defer server.Close()\n    \n    // Start long-running request\n    go makeSlowRequest(server)\n    time.Sleep(100*time.Millisecond)\n    \n    // Trigger shutdown while request is in flight\n    go func() {\n        server.requestShutdown()\n    }()\n    \n    // Wait with generous timeout\n    select {\n    case <-server.Done():\n        // Success\n    case <-time.After(5*time.Second):\n        t.Fatal(\"Shutdown timeout\")\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n### Memory Usage\n- Signal channel: 1-2 signals buffered = negligible overhead\n- Context overhead: Minimal (used in all modern Go code)\n- sync.Once: Single byte per shutdown operation\n\n### Latency\n- Signal detection: <1ms typically (OS-dependent)\n- First component stops: <10ms in well-designed systems\n- Full graceful shutdown: 1-30 seconds (configurable)\n\n### CPU Usage\n- Idle signal handler: 0% CPU\n- During shutdown: Brief spike during cleanup\n- Worst case: One thread per waiting goroutine during timeout\n\n### Best Practices\n- Use context for free cancellation propagation\n- Reserve buffer size of at least 1 for signal channels\n- Set shutdown timeout to 30-60 seconds for most applications\n- Log shutdown events for debugging\n\n---\n\n## Platform-Specific Considerations\n\n### Linux/macOS (POSIX)\n- SIGTERM: Standard container/systemd shutdown signal (use this)\n- SIGINT: Keyboard interrupt (Ctrl+C)\n- SIGHUP: Log rotation signal (Grafana pattern)\n\n### Windows\n- Different signals available (see os.Signal behavior)\n- Consider using context directly instead of signals\n- No SIGHUP equivalent\n\n### Docker/Container\n- Sends SIGTERM on stop (30-second default timeout)\n- Sends SIGKILL if process doesn't exit\n- Implement 15-25 second graceful shutdown\n\n### Systemd\n- Sends SIGTERM to stop service\n- Respects TimeoutStopSec= in service file\n- Can notify readiness with sd_notify\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nChoose your pattern based on:\n\n1. **Simple HTTP service** → Use Grafana pattern (explicit timeout)\n2. **Complex multi-component system** → Use Prometheus pattern (run.Group)\n3. **Microservice/controller** → Use Kubernetes pattern (context)\n\nAll three patterns are proven in production and handle the critical requirement: **graceful shutdown without losing data**.\n\nEOF\ncat /tmp/IMPLEMENTATION_GUIDE.md\n","description":"Create comprehensive implementation > /tmp/COMPREHENSIVE_SUMMARY.md << 'EOF'\n# Graceful Shutdown in Go - Comprehensive Research Summary\n\n## Document Overview\n\nThis document presents a detailed analysis of graceful shutdown patterns found across three production-grade Go projects:\n1. **Kubernetes** - Container orchestration platform\n2. **Prometheus** - Time series database and monitoring system  \n3. **Grafana** - Metrics visualization and alerting platform\n\nAll code examples are extracted from official GitHub repositories and represent current best practices.\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: Core Concepts\n\n### What is Graceful Shutdown?\n\nGraceful shutdown is the process of safely terminating a running application while:\n- Completing in-flight requests\n- Persisting pending data\n- Draining queues\n- Cleaning up resources\n- Notifying dependent systems\n\n### Why It Matters\n\n- **Data Integrity**: Prevents data loss during container restarts\n- **User Experience**: Requests complete rather than timeout\n- **System Health**: Proper cleanup prevents resource leaks\n- **Operational Safety**: Works seamlessly with container orchestration\n\n### Signal-Based Shutdown Flow\n\n```\nOS Signal (SIGTERM) \n    ↓\nSignal Handler (os/signal.Notify)\n    ↓\nContext Cancellation or Channel Communication\n    ↓\nAll Components Informed\n    ↓\nIn-Flight Requests Drained\n    ↓\nBackground Services Stopped\n    ↓\nResources Cleaned Up\n    ↓\nProcess Exits (0 for success, 1 for timeout/error)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Project Analysis\n\n### KUBERNETES: Context-Based Cancellation\n\n**Repository**: github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes  \n**Pattern**: Propagate context.Context through all components\n\n#### Core Files\n\n1. **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go**\n   - Provides `SetupSignalContext() context.Context`\n   - Returns context cancelled on SIGTERM or SIGINT\n   - Guarantees single handler registration (panics if called twice)\n\n2. **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go**\n   - Platform-specific signal definitions\n   - Handles: `os.Interrupt` (SIGINT), `syscall.SIGTERM`\n\n3. **pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go**\n   - Advanced handler with cleanup functions\n   - Guarantees cleanup executes exactly once\n   - Supports multiple signal types\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n| Aspect | Implementation |\n|--------|---|\n| **Signal Handling** | `signal.Notify(ch, shutdownSignals...)` |\n| **Primary Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM |\n| **Coordination** | `context.Context` propagation |\n| **Cleanup Pattern** | Context cancellation |\n| **Timeout** | Implicit (per-component) |\n| **Double Signal** | `os.Exit(1)` on 2nd signal |\n| **Dependencies** | Standard library only |\n\n#### Code Pattern\n\n```go\nfunc SetupSignalContext() context.Context {\n    shutdownHandler := make(chan os.Signal, 2)\n    signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)\n    \n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    go func() {\n        <-shutdownHandler           // 1st signal\n        cancel()\n        <-shutdownHandler           // 2nd signal\n        os.Exit(1)\n    }()\n    return ctx\n}\n\n// Usage in main\nctx := SetupSignalContext()\n<-ctx.Done()  // Blocks until signal\ncleanup()\n```\n\n#### Advantages\n- Simple, elegant design\n- Automatic propagation through function calls\n- Works with existing context APIs\n- Minimal boilerplate\n\n#### Use Cases\n- Controllers and operators\n- Microservices\n- Command-line tools\n- Anything with clear component hierarchy\n\n---\n\n### PROMETHEUS: Goroutine Orchestration\n\n**Repository**: github.com/prometheus/prometheus  \n**Pattern**: Explicit cleanup functions with oklog/run.Group\n\n#### Core File\n\n**cmd/prometheus/main.go** (lines 1151-1340+)\n- Complex multi-component system\n- 20+ goroutines managing different responsibilities\n- Explicit ordering of startup and shutdown\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n| Aspect | Implementation |\n|--------|---|\n| **Signal Handling** | `signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)` |\n| **Primary Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM (plus SIGHUP for reload) |\n| **Coordination** | `oklog/run.Group` |\n| **Cleanup Pattern** | Explicit cleanup functions per component |\n| **Timeout** | Per-component (not global) |\n| **Double Signal** | Natural (run.Group exits) |\n| **Dependencies** | oklog/run library |\n\n#### Code Pattern\n\n```go\ng := run.Group{}\n\n// Signal handler\n{\n    term := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    cancel := make(chan struct{})\n    \n    g.Add(\n        func() error {  // Execute\n            <-term\n            logger.Warn(\"Received OS signal, exiting gracefully...\")\n            close(cancel)\n            return nil\n        },\n        func(error) {  // Interrupt\n            webHandler.SetReady(web.Stopping)\n        },\n    )\n}\n\n// Each component\n{\n    g.Add(\n        func() error { return scrapeManager.Run(...) },\n        func(error) { scrapeManager.Stop() },\n    )\n}\n\ng.Run()  // Blocks until any component exits\n```\n\n#### Features\n\n1. **Multiple Signal Sources**\n   - OS signal (SIGTERM/SIGINT)\n   - Web API request\n   - Internal cancellation\n\n2. **Ordered Cleanup**\n   - Scrape manager stops before TSDB\n   - Rule manager stops (prevents false alerts)\n   - Discovery managers shut down\n   - Cleanup order matters critically\n\n3. **Shutdown Flags**\n   - `notifier.DrainOnShutdown` (default: true)\n   - `tsdb.EnableMemorySnapshotOnShutdown`\n   - `storage.remote.flush-deadline`\n\n#### Advantages\n- Explicit cleanup for each component\n- Clear dependency ordering\n- All cleanups guaranteed to run\n- Fine-grained control\n\n#### Use Cases\n- Complex systems with many components\n- Systems needing explicit ordering\n- Applications with interdependent services\n- Monitoring and observability systems\n\n---\n\n### GRAFANA: Explicit Timeout with sync.Once\n\n**Repository**: github.com/grafana/grafana  \n**Pattern**: Bounded shutdown timeout with single-execution guarantee\n\n#### Core Files\n\n1. **pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go**\n   - Entry point for signal handling\n   - Manages separate channels for SIGTERM/SIGINT vs SIGHUP\n   - Implements 30-second shutdown timeout\n\n2. **pkg/server/server.go**\n   - Main server lifecycle management\n   - `Shutdown(ctx context.Context, reason string) error`\n   - Uses `sync.Once` for single execution guarantee\n   - Systemd integration (NOTIFY_SOCKET)\n\n3. **pkg/api/http_server.go**\n   - HTTP listener management\n   - Graceful HTTP server shutdown\n   - Concurrent listener support (TCP + Unix sockets)\n   - `http.ErrServerClosed` detection\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n| Aspect | Implementation |\n|--------|---|\n| **Signal Handling** | Separate channels for different signals |\n| **Primary Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM (plus SIGHUP for reload) |\n| **Coordination** | Context + sync.Once |\n| **Cleanup Pattern** | sync.Once + context timeout |\n| **Timeout** | Explicit 30 seconds |\n| **Double Signal** | Returns from handler (no force-exit) |\n| **Dependencies** | Standard library + sync/errgroup |\n\n#### Code Pattern\n\n```go\n// Signal handler goroutine\nfunc listenToSystemSignals(ctx context.Context, s gserver) {\n    signalChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(signalChan, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    \n    <-signalChan\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\n    defer cancel()\n    \n    if err := s.Shutdown(ctx, \"System signal\"); err != nil {\n        fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, \"Shutdown timeout\\n\")\n    }\n}\n\n// Server shutdown\nfunc (s *Server) Shutdown(ctx context.Context, reason string) error {\n    var err error\n    s.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n        s.log.Info(\"Shutdown started\", \"reason\", reason)\n        s.managerAdapter.Shutdown(ctx, \"shutdown\")\n        \n        select {\n        case <-ctx.Done():\n            s.log.Warn(\"Timed out\")\n            err = fmt.Errorf(\"timeout\")\n        default:\n            s.log.Debug(\"Shutdown complete\")\n        }\n    })\n    return err\n}\n\n// HTTP server graceful shutdown\ngo func() {\n    <-ctx.Done()\n    hs.httpSrv.Shutdown(context.Background())\n}()\n\nfor _, listener := range listeners {\n    errg.Go(func() error {\n        err := hs.httpSrv.Serve(listener)\n        if errors.Is(err, http.ErrServerClosed) {\n            return nil  // Success\n        }\n        return err\n    })\n}\n```\n\n#### Special Features\n\n1. **Multi-Signal Handling**\n   ```\n   SIGTERM/SIGINT → Graceful shutdown\n   SIGHUP         → Log reload without shutdown\n   ```\n\n2. **Systemd Integration**\n   - Notifies systemd when ready: `notifySystemd(\"READY=1\")`\n   - Reads `NOTIFY_SOCKET` environment variable\n   - Communicates via Unix domain socket\n\n3. **HTTP-Specific Optimizations**\n   - Separate context for HTTP shutdown (no timeout inheritance)\n   - Handles both TCP and Unix socket listeners\n   - Supports HTTP, HTTP/2, HTTPS, and socket schemes\n\n#### Advantages\n- Clear timeout prevents hanging processes\n- Separate signal channels for different purposes\n- Well-integrated with systemd\n- Explicit error handling\n\n#### Use Cases\n- HTTP/REST services\n- Containerized applications\n- Services managed by systemd\n- Applications needing strict shutdown deadlines\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: Comparative Analysis\n\n### Signal Registration\n\nAll three projects use `os/signal.Notify()` with buffered channels:\n\n```go\n// Kubernetes\nshutdownHandler := make(chan os.Signal, 2)\nsignal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)\n\n// Prometheus\nterm := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n\n// Grafana\nsignalChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(signalChan, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n```\n\n**Buffer Size Selection**:\n- Size 2: Kubernetes (buffer for 1st + 2nd signal)\n- Size 1: Prometheus, Grafana (single signal at a time)\n- General: At least 1 to avoid losing signals\n\n### Signals Handled\n\n| Signal | Kubernetes | Prometheus | Grafana | Purpose |\n|--------|-----------|-----------|---------|---------|\n| SIGINT | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ | Terminal interrupt (Ctrl+C) |\n| SIGTERM | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ | Container/systemd shutdown |\n| SIGHUP | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ | Reload config/logs |\n| SIGQUIT | ✓ (util) | ✗ | ✗ | Quit (advanced interrupt handler) |\n\n### Goroutine Coordination Methods\n\n#### Kubernetes: Context Propagation\n```\nSignal → Context.Cancel() → All goroutines see <-ctx.Done()\n```\n**Propagation**: Automatic through call stack  \n**Pros**: Simple, elegant  \n**Cons**: Less explicit about order\n\n#### Prometheus: run.Group\n```\nSignal → run.Group detects exit → Calls all interrupt functions\n```\n**Propagation**: Explicit via g.Add() registration  \n**Pros**: Clear ordering, explicit cleanup  \n**Cons**: External dependency\n\n#### Grafana: sync.Once + Context\n```\nSignal → Shutdown(ctx) → sync.Once ensures single execution\n```\n**Propagation**: Direct method call  \n**Pros**: Predictable, bounded timeout  \n**Cons**: More boilerplate\n\n### Timeout Handling\n\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | Prometheus | Grafana |\n|--------|-----------|-----------|---------|\n| **Timeout Type** | Per-component | Per-component | Global (30s) |\n| **Timeout Value** | Various | Various | 30 seconds |\n| **Timeout Origin** | Component-specific | Component-specific | Explicit WithTimeout |\n| **On Timeout** | Component-dependent | Component-dependent | Error logged, exit 1 |\n| **Advantage** | Flexible | Flexible | Guaranteed exit |\n\n### Cleanup Order Specification\n\n#### Kubernetes\n- Implicit through context propagation\n- Order follows goroutine creation order\n- Easy to get wrong if dependencies unclear\n\n#### Prometheus\n- Explicit in run.Group calls\n- Cleanup functions called in LIFO order\n- Clear and verifiable\n\n#### Grafana\n- Layered: HTTP → Services → Cleanup\n- Each layer has defined timeout\n- Clear separation of concerns\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: Implementation Patterns\n\n### Pattern A: Minimal Context-Based (Kubernetes Style)\n\n**When to use**: Simple applications with clear hierarchy  \n**Complexity**: Low  \n**Lines of code**: ~20\n\n```go\nfunc setupSignal() context.Context {\n    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    go func() {\n        <-ch\n        cancel()\n    }()\n    return ctx\n}\n\nfunc main() {\n    ctx := setupSignal()\n    go func() {\n        select {\n        case <-ctx.Done():\n            cleanup()\n            os.Exit(0)\n        }\n    }()\n    runServer(ctx)\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern B: Goroutine-Orchestrated (Prometheus Style)\n\n**When to use**: Complex systems with many components  \n**Complexity**: Medium  \n**Lines of code**: ~50-100\n\n```go\nimport \"github.com/oklog/run\"\n\nvar g run.Group\n\n// Signal handler\ng.Add(\n    func() error {\n        sig := <-term\n        log.Warn(\"Signal\", \"sig\", sig)\n        return nil\n    },\n    func(error) {\n        log.Info(\"Stopping...\")\n    },\n)\n\n// Each component\ng.Add(\n    func() error { return component.Run() },\n    func(error) { component.Stop() },\n)\n\ng.Run()\n```\n\n### Pattern C: Timeout-Bounded (Grafana Style)\n\n**When to use**: HTTP services needing bounded shutdown  \n**Complexity**: Medium  \n**Lines of code**: ~30\n\n```go\nsig := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(sig, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n\ngo func() {\n    <-sig\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(\n        context.Background(), 30*time.Second)\n    defer cancel()\n    if err := server.Shutdown(ctx); err != nil {\n        log.Error(\"Shutdown timeout\", err)\n    }\n}()\n\nserver.ListenAndServe()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: Best Practices Extracted\n\n### 1. Signal Registration\n\n**DO:**\n- Register early in main()\n- Use buffered channels (size ≥ 1)\n- Register exactly once (use sync.Once or panic)\n- Defer to OS signal delivery until handler ready\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Call signal.Notify() multiple times without cleanup\n- Use unbuffered channels\n- Register late in startup sequence\n- Forget to handle SIGTERM\n\n### 2. Cleanup Ordering\n\n**DO:**\n- Stop accepting connections first\n- Drain in-flight requests second\n- Stop background workers third\n- Flush data to storage last\n- Log each step\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Stop storage before workers finish writing\n- Force-close connections with pending requests\n- Skip cleanup steps\n- Assume goroutines see signal automatically\n\n### 3. Timeout Management\n\n**DO:**\n- Use explicit timeouts (30-60 seconds typical)\n- Context.WithTimeout for bounded operations\n- Log timeout conditions\n- Handle timeout as error case\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Use infinite contexts\n- Expect graceful shutdown without timeout\n- Ignore timeout errors\n- Set timeout too short (<5 seconds)\n\n### 4. Coordination\n\n**DO:**\n- Pass context through call stack\n- Use sync.Once for shutdown code\n- Log shutdown events\n- Test graceful shutdown\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Create \"global\" shutdown flags\n- Rely on goroutine panic for cleanup\n- Forget to wait for goroutine completion\n- Use bare select statements without default case\n\n### 5. Error Handling\n\n**DO:**\n- Log all shutdown errors\n- Distinguish timeout from cancellation\n- Return error status codes appropriately\n- Track shutdown completion\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Silently ignore shutdown errors\n- Exit immediately on first error\n- Lose error context\n- Mix error types\n\n### 6. Testing\n\n**DO:**\n- Test graceful shutdown explicitly\n- Simulate signals in tests\n- Verify cleanup runs\n- Test timeout conditions\n- Verify no data loss\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Skip shutdown testing\n- Only test happy path\n- Assume cleanup works\n- Test with real signals in CI\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Common Pitfalls and Solutions\n\n### Pitfall 1: Lost Signals\n```go\n// WRONG - unbuffered channel loses signals\nsig := make(chan os.Signal)\nsignal.Notify(sig, syscall.SIGTERM)\n\n// CORRECT - buffered channel preserves signals\nsig := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(sig, syscall.SIGTERM)\n```\n\n### Pitfall 2: Infinite Waiting\n```go\n// WRONG - can block forever\nserver.Shutdown(context.Background())\n\n// CORRECT - bounded wait\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 30*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\nserver.Shutdown(ctx)\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Goroutine Leaks\n```go\n// WRONG - goroutine never exits\ngo func() {\n    for {\n        doWork()\n    }\n}()\n\n// CORRECT - responds to context\ngo func() {\n    for {\n        select {\n        case <-ctx.Done():\n            return\n        case <-workChan:\n            doWork()\n        }\n    }\n}()\n```\n\n### Pitfall 4: Race Conditions\n```go\n// WRONG - concurrent shutdown calls\ns.shutdown()\ns.shutdown()  // Called again\n\n// CORRECT - synchronized with sync.Once\ns.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n    s.shutdown()\n})\n```\n\n### Pitfall 5: Lost Context\n```go\n// WRONG - inner function ignores context\nfunc handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {\n    time.Sleep(10*time.Second)  // Can't be interrupted\n}\n\n// CORRECT - respects context\nfunc handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {\n    select {\n    case <-ctx.Done():\n        return\n    case <-time.After(10*time.Second):\n        // Process result\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: File Reference Guide\n\n### Kubernetes Files\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |\n|------|---------|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go` | Core signal handler | `SetupSignalContext()` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go` | POSIX signals | `shutdownSignals` |\n| `pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go` | Advanced interrupt handler | `Handler`, `Run()` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal.go` | Template | Reference implementation |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/leader-election/main.go` | Leader election pattern | Complete example |\n\n### Prometheus Files\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |\n|------|---------|---|\n| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Signal handling + orchestration | `run.Group`, signal handlers (lines 1151+) |\n| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Feature flags | `DrainOnShutdown` (line 582) |\n| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Memory snapshot | `EnableMemorySnapshotOnShutdown` (line 234) |\n\n### Grafana Files\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |\n|------|---------|---|\n| `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` | Signal listener | `listenToSystemSignals()` (lines 148-170) |\n| `pkg/server/server.go` | Server lifecycle | `Shutdown()`, `notifySystemd()` |\n| `pkg/api/http_server.go` | HTTP shutdown | `Start()`, graceful shutdown (lines 490+) |\n\n---\n\n## Part 8: Conclusion\n\nAll three projects implement graceful shutdown successfully using:\n\n1. **Core Signal Handling**: `os/signal.Notify()` with buffered channels\n2. **Signals**: SIGTERM and SIGINT for shutdown, SIGHUP for reload\n3. **Coordination**: Context, run.Group, or sync.Once depending on complexity\n4. **Cleanup**: Ordered shutdown of components, draining before stopping\n5. **Timeouts**: Explicit bounds to prevent hanging processes\n\n**Choose your pattern based on needs:**\n\n| Requirement | Best Pattern |\n|------------|---|\n| Simple service with few components | **Kubernetes (context)** |\n| Complex system with many services | **Prometheus (run.Group)** |\n| HTTP service needing strict timeout | **Grafana (explicit timeout)** |\n| Learning/reference implementation | **Kubernetes sample-controller** |\n\nAll three patterns are production-proven and handle the critical requirement: **graceful shutdown without losing data**.\n\nEOF\ncat /tmp/COMPREHENSIVE_SUMMARY.md\n","description":"Create final comprehensive summary {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01X4vuce7qQNMXdKomXJ5bo1","type":"tool_result","content":"# Graceful Shutdown in Go - Comprehensive Research Summary\n\n## Document Overview\n\nThis document presents a detailed analysis of graceful shutdown patterns found across three production-grade Go projects:\n1. **Kubernetes** - Container orchestration platform\n2. **Prometheus** - Time series database and monitoring system  \n3. **Grafana** - Metrics visualization and alerting platform\n\nAll code examples are extracted from official GitHub repositories and represent current best practices.\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: Core Concepts\n\n### What is Graceful Shutdown?\n\nGraceful shutdown is the process of safely terminating a running application while:\n- Completing in-flight requests\n- Persisting pending data\n- Draining queues\n- Cleaning up resources\n- Notifying dependent systems\n\n### Why It Matters\n\n- **Data Integrity**: Prevents data loss during container restarts\n- **User Experience**: Requests complete rather than timeout\n- **System Health**: Proper cleanup prevents resource leaks\n- **Operational Safety**: Works seamlessly with container orchestration\n\n### Signal-Based Shutdown Flow\n\n```\nOS Signal (SIGTERM) \n    ↓\nSignal Handler (os/signal.Notify)\n    ↓\nContext Cancellation or Channel Communication\n    ↓\nAll Components Informed\n    ↓\nIn-Flight Requests Drained\n    ↓\nBackground Services Stopped\n    ↓\nResources Cleaned Up\n    ↓\nProcess Exits (0 for success, 1 for timeout/error)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Project Analysis\n\n### KUBERNETES: Context-Based Cancellation\n\n**Repository**: github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes  \n**Pattern**: Propagate context.Context through all components\n\n#### Core Files\n\n1. **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go**\n   - Provides `SetupSignalContext() context.Context`\n   - Returns context cancelled on SIGTERM or SIGINT\n   - Guarantees single handler registration (panics if called twice)\n\n2. **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go**\n   - Platform-specific signal definitions\n   - Handles: `os.Interrupt` (SIGINT), `syscall.SIGTERM`\n\n3. **pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go**\n   - Advanced handler with cleanup functions\n   - Guarantees cleanup executes exactly once\n   - Supports multiple signal types\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n| Aspect | Implementation |\n|--------|---|\n| **Signal Handling** | `signal.Notify(ch, shutdownSignals...)` |\n| **Primary Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM |\n| **Coordination** | `context.Context` propagation |\n| **Cleanup Pattern** | Context cancellation |\n| **Timeout** | Implicit (per-component) |\n| **Double Signal** | `os.Exit(1)` on 2nd signal |\n| **Dependencies** | Standard library only |\n\n#### Code Pattern\n\n```go\nfunc SetupSignalContext() context.Context {\n    shutdownHandler := make(chan os.Signal, 2)\n    signal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)\n    \n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    go func() {\n        <-shutdownHandler           // 1st signal\n        cancel()\n        <-shutdownHandler           // 2nd signal\n        os.Exit(1)\n    }()\n    return ctx\n}\n\n// Usage in main\nctx := SetupSignalContext()\n<-ctx.Done()  // Blocks until signal\ncleanup()\n```\n\n#### Advantages\n- Simple, elegant design\n- Automatic propagation through function calls\n- Works with existing context APIs\n- Minimal boilerplate\n\n#### Use Cases\n- Controllers and operators\n- Microservices\n- Command-line tools\n- Anything with clear component hierarchy\n\n---\n\n### PROMETHEUS: Goroutine Orchestration\n\n**Repository**: github.com/prometheus/prometheus  \n**Pattern**: Explicit cleanup functions with oklog/run.Group\n\n#### Core File\n\n**cmd/prometheus/main.go** (lines 1151-1340+)\n- Complex multi-component system\n- 20+ goroutines managing different responsibilities\n- Explicit ordering of startup and shutdown\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n| Aspect | Implementation |\n|--------|---|\n| **Signal Handling** | `signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)` |\n| **Primary Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM (plus SIGHUP for reload) |\n| **Coordination** | `oklog/run.Group` |\n| **Cleanup Pattern** | Explicit cleanup functions per component |\n| **Timeout** | Per-component (not global) |\n| **Double Signal** | Natural (run.Group exits) |\n| **Dependencies** | oklog/run library |\n\n#### Code Pattern\n\n```go\ng := run.Group{}\n\n// Signal handler\n{\n    term := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    cancel := make(chan struct{})\n    \n    g.Add(\n        func() error {  // Execute\n            <-term\n            logger.Warn(\"Received OS signal, exiting gracefully...\")\n            close(cancel)\n            return nil\n        },\n        func(error) {  // Interrupt\n            webHandler.SetReady(web.Stopping)\n        },\n    )\n}\n\n// Each component\n{\n    g.Add(\n        func() error { return scrapeManager.Run(...) },\n        func(error) { scrapeManager.Stop() },\n    )\n}\n\ng.Run()  // Blocks until any component exits\n```\n\n#### Features\n\n1. **Multiple Signal Sources**\n   - OS signal (SIGTERM/SIGINT)\n   - Web API request\n   - Internal cancellation\n\n2. **Ordered Cleanup**\n   - Scrape manager stops before TSDB\n   - Rule manager stops (prevents false alerts)\n   - Discovery managers shut down\n   - Cleanup order matters critically\n\n3. **Shutdown Flags**\n   - `notifier.DrainOnShutdown` (default: true)\n   - `tsdb.EnableMemorySnapshotOnShutdown`\n   - `storage.remote.flush-deadline`\n\n#### Advantages\n- Explicit cleanup for each component\n- Clear dependency ordering\n- All cleanups guaranteed to run\n- Fine-grained control\n\n#### Use Cases\n- Complex systems with many components\n- Systems needing explicit ordering\n- Applications with interdependent services\n- Monitoring and observability systems\n\n---\n\n### GRAFANA: Explicit Timeout with sync.Once\n\n**Repository**: github.com/grafana/grafana  \n**Pattern**: Bounded shutdown timeout with single-execution guarantee\n\n#### Core Files\n\n1. **pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go**\n   - Entry point for signal handling\n   - Manages separate channels for SIGTERM/SIGINT vs SIGHUP\n   - Implements 30-second shutdown timeout\n\n2. **pkg/server/server.go**\n   - Main server lifecycle management\n   - `Shutdown(ctx context.Context, reason string) error`\n   - Uses `sync.Once` for single execution guarantee\n   - Systemd integration (NOTIFY_SOCKET)\n\n3. **pkg/api/http_server.go**\n   - HTTP listener management\n   - Graceful HTTP server shutdown\n   - Concurrent listener support (TCP + Unix sockets)\n   - `http.ErrServerClosed` detection\n\n#### Key Characteristics\n\n| Aspect | Implementation |\n|--------|---|\n| **Signal Handling** | Separate channels for different signals |\n| **Primary Signals** | SIGINT, SIGTERM (plus SIGHUP for reload) |\n| **Coordination** | Context + sync.Once |\n| **Cleanup Pattern** | sync.Once + context timeout |\n| **Timeout** | Explicit 30 seconds |\n| **Double Signal** | Returns from handler (no force-exit) |\n| **Dependencies** | Standard library + sync/errgroup |\n\n#### Code Pattern\n\n```go\n// Signal handler goroutine\nfunc listenToSystemSignals(ctx context.Context, s gserver) {\n    signalChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(signalChan, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    \n    <-signalChan\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\n    defer cancel()\n    \n    if err := s.Shutdown(ctx, \"System signal\"); err != nil {\n        fmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, \"Shutdown timeout\\n\")\n    }\n}\n\n// Server shutdown\nfunc (s *Server) Shutdown(ctx context.Context, reason string) error {\n    var err error\n    s.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n        s.log.Info(\"Shutdown started\", \"reason\", reason)\n        s.managerAdapter.Shutdown(ctx, \"shutdown\")\n        \n        select {\n        case <-ctx.Done():\n            s.log.Warn(\"Timed out\")\n            err = fmt.Errorf(\"timeout\")\n        default:\n            s.log.Debug(\"Shutdown complete\")\n        }\n    })\n    return err\n}\n\n// HTTP server graceful shutdown\ngo func() {\n    <-ctx.Done()\n    hs.httpSrv.Shutdown(context.Background())\n}()\n\nfor _, listener := range listeners {\n    errg.Go(func() error {\n        err := hs.httpSrv.Serve(listener)\n        if errors.Is(err, http.ErrServerClosed) {\n            return nil  // Success\n        }\n        return err\n    })\n}\n```\n\n#### Special Features\n\n1. **Multi-Signal Handling**\n   ```\n   SIGTERM/SIGINT → Graceful shutdown\n   SIGHUP         → Log reload without shutdown\n   ```\n\n2. **Systemd Integration**\n   - Notifies systemd when ready: `notifySystemd(\"READY=1\")`\n   - Reads `NOTIFY_SOCKET` environment variable\n   - Communicates via Unix domain socket\n\n3. **HTTP-Specific Optimizations**\n   - Separate context for HTTP shutdown (no timeout inheritance)\n   - Handles both TCP and Unix socket listeners\n   - Supports HTTP, HTTP/2, HTTPS, and socket schemes\n\n#### Advantages\n- Clear timeout prevents hanging processes\n- Separate signal channels for different purposes\n- Well-integrated with systemd\n- Explicit error handling\n\n#### Use Cases\n- HTTP/REST services\n- Containerized applications\n- Services managed by systemd\n- Applications needing strict shutdown deadlines\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: Comparative Analysis\n\n### Signal Registration\n\nAll three projects use `os/signal.Notify()` with buffered channels:\n\n```go\n// Kubernetes\nshutdownHandler := make(chan os.Signal, 2)\nsignal.Notify(shutdownHandler, shutdownSignals...)\n\n// Prometheus\nterm := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n\n// Grafana\nsignalChan := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(signalChan, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n```\n\n**Buffer Size Selection**:\n- Size 2: Kubernetes (buffer for 1st + 2nd signal)\n- Size 1: Prometheus, Grafana (single signal at a time)\n- General: At least 1 to avoid losing signals\n\n### Signals Handled\n\n| Signal | Kubernetes | Prometheus | Grafana | Purpose |\n|--------|-----------|-----------|---------|---------|\n| SIGINT | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ | Terminal interrupt (Ctrl+C) |\n| SIGTERM | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ | Container/systemd shutdown |\n| SIGHUP | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ | Reload config/logs |\n| SIGQUIT | ✓ (util) | ✗ | ✗ | Quit (advanced interrupt handler) |\n\n### Goroutine Coordination Methods\n\n#### Kubernetes: Context Propagation\n```\nSignal → Context.Cancel() → All goroutines see <-ctx.Done()\n```\n**Propagation**: Automatic through call stack  \n**Pros**: Simple, elegant  \n**Cons**: Less explicit about order\n\n#### Prometheus: run.Group\n```\nSignal → run.Group detects exit → Calls all interrupt functions\n```\n**Propagation**: Explicit via g.Add() registration  \n**Pros**: Clear ordering, explicit cleanup  \n**Cons**: External dependency\n\n#### Grafana: sync.Once + Context\n```\nSignal → Shutdown(ctx) → sync.Once ensures single execution\n```\n**Propagation**: Direct method call  \n**Pros**: Predictable, bounded timeout  \n**Cons**: More boilerplate\n\n### Timeout Handling\n\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | Prometheus | Grafana |\n|--------|-----------|-----------|---------|\n| **Timeout Type** | Per-component | Per-component | Global (30s) |\n| **Timeout Value** | Various | Various | 30 seconds |\n| **Timeout Origin** | Component-specific | Component-specific | Explicit WithTimeout |\n| **On Timeout** | Component-dependent | Component-dependent | Error logged, exit 1 |\n| **Advantage** | Flexible | Flexible | Guaranteed exit |\n\n### Cleanup Order Specification\n\n#### Kubernetes\n- Implicit through context propagation\n- Order follows goroutine creation order\n- Easy to get wrong if dependencies unclear\n\n#### Prometheus\n- Explicit in run.Group calls\n- Cleanup functions called in LIFO order\n- Clear and verifiable\n\n#### Grafana\n- Layered: HTTP → Services → Cleanup\n- Each layer has defined timeout\n- Clear separation of concerns\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: Implementation Patterns\n\n### Pattern A: Minimal Context-Based (Kubernetes Style)\n\n**When to use**: Simple applications with clear hierarchy  \n**Complexity**: Low  \n**Lines of code**: ~20\n\n```go\nfunc setupSignal() context.Context {\n    ch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\n    signal.Notify(ch, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n    go func() {\n        <-ch\n        cancel()\n    }()\n    return ctx\n}\n\nfunc main() {\n    ctx := setupSignal()\n    go func() {\n        select {\n        case <-ctx.Done():\n            cleanup()\n            os.Exit(0)\n        }\n    }()\n    runServer(ctx)\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern B: Goroutine-Orchestrated (Prometheus Style)\n\n**When to use**: Complex systems with many components  \n**Complexity**: Medium  \n**Lines of code**: ~50-100\n\n```go\nimport \"github.com/oklog/run\"\n\nvar g run.Group\n\n// Signal handler\ng.Add(\n    func() error {\n        sig := <-term\n        log.Warn(\"Signal\", \"sig\", sig)\n        return nil\n    },\n    func(error) {\n        log.Info(\"Stopping...\")\n    },\n)\n\n// Each component\ng.Add(\n    func() error { return component.Run() },\n    func(error) { component.Stop() },\n)\n\ng.Run()\n```\n\n### Pattern C: Timeout-Bounded (Grafana Style)\n\n**When to use**: HTTP services needing bounded shutdown  \n**Complexity**: Medium  \n**Lines of code**: ~30\n\n```go\nsig := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(sig, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)\n\ngo func() {\n    <-sig\n    ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(\n        context.Background(), 30*time.Second)\n    defer cancel()\n    if err := server.Shutdown(ctx); err != nil {\n        log.Error(\"Shutdown timeout\", err)\n    }\n}()\n\nserver.ListenAndServe()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: Best Practices Extracted\n\n### 1. Signal Registration\n\n**DO:**\n- Register early in main()\n- Use buffered channels (size ≥ 1)\n- Register exactly once (use sync.Once or panic)\n- Defer to OS signal delivery until handler ready\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Call signal.Notify() multiple times without cleanup\n- Use unbuffered channels\n- Register late in startup sequence\n- Forget to handle SIGTERM\n\n### 2. Cleanup Ordering\n\n**DO:**\n- Stop accepting connections first\n- Drain in-flight requests second\n- Stop background workers third\n- Flush data to storage last\n- Log each step\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Stop storage before workers finish writing\n- Force-close connections with pending requests\n- Skip cleanup steps\n- Assume goroutines see signal automatically\n\n### 3. Timeout Management\n\n**DO:**\n- Use explicit timeouts (30-60 seconds typical)\n- Context.WithTimeout for bounded operations\n- Log timeout conditions\n- Handle timeout as error case\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Use infinite contexts\n- Expect graceful shutdown without timeout\n- Ignore timeout errors\n- Set timeout too short (<5 seconds)\n\n### 4. Coordination\n\n**DO:**\n- Pass context through call stack\n- Use sync.Once for shutdown code\n- Log shutdown events\n- Test graceful shutdown\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Create \"global\" shutdown flags\n- Rely on goroutine panic for cleanup\n- Forget to wait for goroutine completion\n- Use bare select statements without default case\n\n### 5. Error Handling\n\n**DO:**\n- Log all shutdown errors\n- Distinguish timeout from cancellation\n- Return error status codes appropriately\n- Track shutdown completion\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Silently ignore shutdown errors\n- Exit immediately on first error\n- Lose error context\n- Mix error types\n\n### 6. Testing\n\n**DO:**\n- Test graceful shutdown explicitly\n- Simulate signals in tests\n- Verify cleanup runs\n- Test timeout conditions\n- Verify no data loss\n\n**DON'T:**\n- Skip shutdown testing\n- Only test happy path\n- Assume cleanup works\n- Test with real signals in CI\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Common Pitfalls and Solutions\n\n### Pitfall 1: Lost Signals\n```go\n// WRONG - unbuffered channel loses signals\nsig := make(chan os.Signal)\nsignal.Notify(sig, syscall.SIGTERM)\n\n// CORRECT - buffered channel preserves signals\nsig := make(chan os.Signal, 1)\nsignal.Notify(sig, syscall.SIGTERM)\n```\n\n### Pitfall 2: Infinite Waiting\n```go\n// WRONG - can block forever\nserver.Shutdown(context.Background())\n\n// CORRECT - bounded wait\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), 30*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\nserver.Shutdown(ctx)\n```\n\n### Pitfall 3: Goroutine Leaks\n```go\n// WRONG - goroutine never exits\ngo func() {\n    for {\n        doWork()\n    }\n}()\n\n// CORRECT - responds to context\ngo func() {\n    for {\n        select {\n        case <-ctx.Done():\n            return\n        case <-workChan:\n            doWork()\n        }\n    }\n}()\n```\n\n### Pitfall 4: Race Conditions\n```go\n// WRONG - concurrent shutdown calls\ns.shutdown()\ns.shutdown()  // Called again\n\n// CORRECT - synchronized with sync.Once\ns.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n    s.shutdown()\n})\n```\n\n### Pitfall 5: Lost Context\n```go\n// WRONG - inner function ignores context\nfunc handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {\n    time.Sleep(10*time.Second)  // Can't be interrupted\n}\n\n// CORRECT - respects context\nfunc handleRequest(ctx context.Context) {\n    select {\n    case <-ctx.Done():\n        return\n    case <-time.After(10*time.Second):\n        // Process result\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: File Reference Guide\n\n### Kubernetes Files\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |\n|------|---------|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go` | Core signal handler | `SetupSignalContext()` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go` | POSIX signals | `shutdownSignals` |\n| `pkg/util/interrupt/interrupt.go` | Advanced interrupt handler | `Handler`, `Run()` |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal.go` | Template | Reference implementation |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/leader-election/main.go` | Leader election pattern | Complete example |\n\n### Prometheus Files\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |\n|------|---------|---|\n| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Signal handling + orchestration | `run.Group`, signal handlers (lines 1151+) |\n| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Feature flags | `DrainOnShutdown` (line 582) |\n| `cmd/prometheus/main.go` | Memory snapshot | `EnableMemorySnapshotOnShutdown` (line 234) |\n\n### Grafana Files\n\n| File | Purpose | Key Symbols |\n|------|---------|---|\n| `pkg/cmd/grafana-server/commands/cli.go` | Signal listener | `listenToSystemSignals()` (lines 148-170) |\n| `pkg/server/server.go` | Server lifecycle | `Shutdown()`, `notifySystemd()` |\n| `pkg/api/http_server.go` | HTTP shutdown | `Start()`, graceful shutdown (lines 490+) |\n\n---\n\n## Part 8: Conclusion\n\nAll three projects implement graceful shutdown successfully using:\n\n1. **Core Signal Handling**: `os/signal.Notify()` with buffered channels\n2. **Signals**: SIGTERM and SIGINT for shutdown, SIGHUP for reload\n3. **Coordination**: Context, run.Group, or sync.Once depending on complexity\n4. **Cleanup**: Ordered shutdown of components, draining before stopping\n5. **Timeouts**: Explicit bounds to prevent hanging processes\n\n**Choose your pattern based on needs:**\n\n| Requirement | Best Pattern |\n|------------|---|\n| Simple service with few components | **Kubernetes (context)** |\n| Complex system with many services | **Prometheus (run.Group)** |\n| HTTP service needing strict timeout | **Grafana (explicit timeout)** |\n| Learning/reference implementation | **Kubernetes sample-controller** |\n\nAll three patterns are production-proven and handle the critical requirement: **graceful shutdown without losing Use Buffered Channels\n```go\nch := make(chan os.Signal, 1)  // Don't use unbuffered\nsignal.Notify(ch, syscall.SIGTERM, os.Interrupt)\n```\n\n### 2. Always Use Timeout\n```go\nctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(ctx, 30*time.Second)\ndefer cancel()\nserver.Shutdown(ctx)  // Won't hang forever\n```\n\n### 3. Ensure Single Execution\n```go\ns.shutdownOnce.Do(func() {\n    // This code runs exactly once\n})\n```\n\n### 4. Log Everything\n```go\nlogger.Info(\"Shutdown started\", \"reason\", reason)\nlogger.Warn(\"Timed out waiting for shutdown\")\nlogger.Info(\"Shutdown complete\")\n```\n\n### 5. Pass Context Through Call Stack\n```go\nfunc handler(ctx context.Context) {\n    select {\n    case <-ctx.Done():\n        return  // Responds to cancellation\n    case <-workChan:\n        doWork()\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Recommended Reading Order\n\n### For Quick Implementation (30 minutes)\n1. Comprehensive Research Summary\n\n## Document Overview\n\nThis document presents a detailed analysis of graceful shutdown patterns found across three production-grade Go projects:\n1. **Kubernetes** - Container orchestration platform\n2. **Prometheus** - Time series database and monitoring system  \n3. **Grafana** - Metrics visualization and alerting platform\n\nAll code examples are extracted from official GitHub repositories and represent current best practices.\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: Core Concepts\n\n### What is Graceful Shutdown?\n\nGraceful shutdown is the process of safely terminating a running application while:\n- Completing in-flight requests\n- Persisting pending data\n- Draining queues\n- Cleaning up resources\n- Notifying dependent systems\n\n### Why It Matters\n\n- **Data Integrity**: Prevents data loss during container restarts\n- **User Experience**: Requests complete rather than timeout\n- **System Health**: Proper cleanup prevents resource leaks\n- **Operational Safety**: Works seamlessly with container orchestration\n\n### Signal-Based Shutdown Flow\n\n```\nOS Signal (SIGTERM) \n    ↓\nSignal Handler (os/signal.Notify)\n    ↓\nContext Cancellation or Channel Communication\n    ↓\nAll Components Informed\n    ↓\nIn-Flight Requests Drained\n    ↓\nBackground Services Stopped\n    ↓\nResources Cleaned Up\n    ↓\nProcess Exits (0 for success, 1 for timeout/error)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Project Analysis\n\n### KUBERNETES: Context-Based Cancellation\n\n**Repository**: github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes  \n**Pattern**: Propagate context.Context through all components\n\n#### Core Files\n\n1. **staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal.go**\n   - The signal handler is protected by `onlyOneSignalHandler` which panics if called twice, ensuring single execution.\\n\\nThe companion file `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/server/signal_posix.go` defines `shutdownSignals` as `{os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM}` for non-Windows systems. This handler manages `terminationSignals` (SIGHUP, SIGINT, SIGTERM, SIGQUIT) and uses `sync.Once` internally to ensure cleanup functions execute exactly once.\\n\\nThe reference implementation in `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/pkg/signals/signal.go` and `signal_posix.go` demonstrates the standard pattern, while `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/examples/leader-election/main.go` shows how context propagation enables automatic cleanup when contexts are cancelled.\\n\\n**PROMETHEUS/PROMETHEUS** uses explicit goroutine orchestration via the oklog/run library:\\n\\nAt `cmd/prometheus/main.go` (lines 1151-1176), a buffered channel `term` receives signals via `signal.Notify(term, os.Interrupt, syscall.SIGTERM)`. Each service registers with `g.Add(execute func() error, interrupt func(error))`, providing both a function to run and an interrupt handler. When any component exits or a signal arrives, the run.Group calls all registered interrupt functions in reverse registration order, enabling precise cleanup ordering. The shutdown method delegates to `managerAdapter.Shutdown()` for background services and waits on context completion (lines 162-168), logging timeouts if they occur. HTTP graceful shutdown at `pkg/api/http_server.go` (lines 490-497) waits for context cancellation then calls `httpSrv.Shutdown()` with a fresh background context, using `http.ErrServerClosed` detection. The choice between patterns reflects architectural needs: Kubernetes favors simplicity through context propagation, Prometheus requires explicit component ordering, and Grafana emphasizes timeout guarantees for HTTP services.
